        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141433240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10551876575711107675">The Declaration is set in the UK in the future. A future where resources are scarce and people live forever, thanks to the wonder drug Longevity. In order to be eligible to take Longevity, people have to sign the Declaration, stating they will never have any children...although there are some who have broken the rules. These children are called Surpluses, they are seen as a drain on precious resources and they need to work in order to replay their debt to society, and atone for the sins of their</span>
  <span id="freeText10551876575711107675" style="display:none">The Declaration is set in the UK in the future. A future where resources are scarce and people live forever, thanks to the wonder drug Longevity. In order to be eligible to take Longevity, people have to sign the Declaration, stating they will never have any children...although there are some who have broken the rules. These children are called Surpluses, they are seen as a drain on precious resources and they need to work in order to replay their debt to society, and atone for the sins of their parents. Anna is one of these children, having spent most of her life in Grange Hall, she is destined to be a Valuable Asset and is hoping to gain employment as a housekeeper. Her life is turned upside down when a new Surplus, Peter arrives at Grange Hall, he has been living on the outside as an illegal for too many years. He has wild ideas about the Authorities, Surpluses and the wonder drug Longevity, he challenges everything being taught to the Surpluses at Grange Hall and also claims to know Anna's parents!<br /><br />I thought this was a great book, really made you stop and think about how the world truly works! Very realistic and believable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10551876575711107675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152870670?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briana Grenert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briana Grenert" href="/user/show/3054250-briana-grenert">Briana Grenert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer152870670&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152870670" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7899809002298204591">I really like the characters and the book was interesting and thought provoking. I did not suspect that Peter would be Mrs. Princeton's son! The premise was fascinating and the book moved quickly. The setting was adequately explored without the book being lengthy and the language complemented the message. The ending was suitable, though I can't help but feel as if something is missing. That is why I did not give it five stars: there was something more I wanted. However, that aside, I loved this </span>
  <span id="freeText7899809002298204591" style="display:none">I really like the characters and the book was interesting and thought provoking. I did not suspect that Peter would be Mrs. Princeton's son! The premise was fascinating and the book moved quickly. The setting was adequately explored without the book being lengthy and the language complemented the message. The ending was suitable, though I can't help but feel as if something is missing. That is why I did not give it five stars: there was something more I wanted. However, that aside, I loved this book. It is one of those books that I want a sequel for, but at the same time, don't. It was very thought provoking. Just today in biology we were discussing genetic engineering and how that could extend life. Because of this book, extending life even to 200 years seemed less desirable to me. It also caused me to think about what I would have chosen, what I would have done if I were Mrs. Sharpe or Shela of any of the characters. <br />I did not like Shela. She is a little prig...<br />A good book, I highly recommend it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7899809002298204591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GEstiBPsVH2vChwLwxO1kx8a8DyaA+Q2iN62mrnCLzsibURaqLKdFQghqGo05r9MyUUX9FSOalHToPArdIHdoQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MJbL0B20HmVKoXBaJrKAsT2P7Gzd2BG7uWugRKlJRoYKsKICpurXDe2KxDvRR4pu69ALpBNVn9ziFeb1ZAq0HA==')})
  }
